## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: nonlinear dynamics / classical mechanics (nonlinear oscillations)
**Analysis**: The target dv_dt is acceleration with state variables x (position) and v (velocity), matching second-order oscillator equations rewritten as a first-order system. Nonlinear harmonic oscillators commonly include restoring forces depending nonlinearly on x, damping depending on v, and possible explicit time-dependent driving or parametric terms in t.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Simple harmonic oscillator (linear restoring): dv_dt = -c0 * x (undamped conservative linear oscillator)
- Damped harmonic oscillator (linear damping): dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v (viscous damping)
- Driven damped oscillator (additive forcing): dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v + c2 * cos(c3 * t) (external periodic drive)
- Pendulum-type restoring (geometric nonlinearity): dv_dt = -c0 * sin(x) - c1 * v (large-angle pendulum with damping)
- Duffing oscillator (cubic stiffness): dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x**3 - c2 * v (hardening/softening spring with damping)
- Duffing with periodic forcing: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x**3 - c2 * v + c3 * sin(c4 * t) (nonlinear resonance/chaos regimes)
- Quadratic/cubic damping (aerodynamic-like): dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v - c2 * Abs(v) * v (drag increasing with speed)
- Nonlinear stiffness with magnitude dependence: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * Abs(x) * x - c2 * v (piecewise-linear/contact-like stiffness)
- Van der Pol oscillator (self-excited limit cycle): dv_dt = c0 * (1 - c1 * x**2) * v - c2 * x (negative damping at small amplitude, positive at large)
- Rayleigh oscillator (velocity-dependent self-excitation): dv_dt = -c0 * x + c1 * v - c2 * v**3 (limit-cycle from nonlinear damping in v)
- Parametrically excited oscillator (time-varying stiffness): dv_dt = -(c0 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) * x - c3 * v (Mathieu-type parametric resonance)
- Softening via saturating restoring force: dv_dt = -(c0 * x) / (1 + c1 * x**2) - c2 * v (restoring force that saturates at large |x|)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Conservative oscillator behavior → dv_dt depends primarily on x (e.g., -c0*x, -c0*sin(x)) with little/no v term, indicating energy exchange between x and v.
- Viscous dissipation → include a linear -c*v term; the sign should oppose v to remove energy and produce decay to equilibrium.
- Amplitude-dependent frequency (backbone curve) → add odd stiffness nonlinearities in x (x**3, Abs(x)*x); these shift frequency with amplitude (hardening/softening).
- Geometric nonlinearity/angle wrap → use sin(x) (or truncated series x - c*x**3) instead of polynomial restoring force when x is an angle-like coordinate.
- Self-excited limit cycles → use state-dependent damping like (1 - c*x**2)*v or v - c*v**3, yielding negative damping at small amplitude and stabilizing damping at large amplitude.
- Velocity-dependent drag beyond Stokes regime → use Abs(v)*v or v**3 terms to model quadratic/cubic dissipation at higher speeds.
- Parametric resonance signatures → make the coefficient of x explicitly time-dependent, e.g., -(c0 + c1*cos(c2*t))*x, rather than adding forcing as a separate term.
- External periodic forcing → additive sin(c*t) or cos(c*t) terms; near-resonant forcing typically competes with damping (-c*v) and restoring (-c*x).
- Contact/impact or piecewise stiffness → prefer Abs(x)*x or other magnitude-sensitive restoring terms to represent different stiffness for large deflections while preserving symmetry.

\[

\]
Key required structures:
- a **linear** term in \(v\) (odd, smooth): \(\propto v\)
- a **log** term \(\log(|v|+1)\) (even in \(v\), non-polynomial, non-analytic at \(v=0\) due to \(|v|\))
- a **pure** cubic in \(x\): \(\propto x^3\) (no \(x\), \(x|x|\), \(x^2\), \(x^5\), etc.)
- a **pure sinusoid** in \(t\) with **constant amplitude**: \(\propto \sin(t)\) (no \(e^{kt}\) amplitude modulation)

So any candidate must be able to produce simultaneously:
1) \(\log(|v|+1)\) specifically (log of \(|v|+\text{const}\)),  
2) a standalone \(v\) term,  
3) a standalone \(\sin(t)\) term with constant amplitude,  
4) only \(x^3\) in \(x\).

Now check candidates:
